  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer8887332636915872742">How do you outwit a Twit? Mr. and Mrs. Twit are the smelliest, ugliest people in the world. They hate everything -- except playing mean jokes on each other, catching innocent birds to put in their Bird Pies, and making their caged monkeys, the Muggle-Wumps, stand on their heads all day. But the Muggle-Wumps have had enough. They don't just want out, they want revenge.</span>

<div id="review_2430944489" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2430944489" />
    <a title="JV (semi-hiatus)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus"><img alt="JV (semi-hiatus)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559624981p2/20906165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2430944489?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JV (semi-hiatus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JV (semi-hiatus)" href="/user/show/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus">JV (semi-hiatus)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18827187-the-twits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=home-for-my-heart">home-for-my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=for-my-little-dean">for-my-little-dean</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=kids-these-days">kids-these-days</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2430944489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10216085047512611152">I feel full of the joys of spring! This was such a delightful little book. My morbid, inner kid couldn't have been more ecstatic! Should I call someone a twit or a nitwit? I guess, no. That would be very rude of me! My doppelgänger would approve otherwise. And since I'm not like my sinister doppelgänger, I would leave all the sheer nastiness to him along with Mr. and Mrs. Twit, who are also quite repulsive, if you ask me. I'd rather have pleasant thoughts rather than wicked ones.<blockquote>
  <i>"If a person </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10216085047512611152" style="display:none">I feel full of the joys of spring! This was such a delightful little book. My morbid, inner kid couldn't have been more ecstatic! Should I call someone a twit or a nitwit? I guess, no. That would be very rude of me! My doppelgänger would approve otherwise. And since I'm not like my sinister doppelgänger, I would leave all the sheer nastiness to him along with Mr. and Mrs. Twit, who are also quite repulsive, if you ask me. I'd rather have pleasant thoughts rather than wicked ones.<blockquote>
  <i>"If a person has ugly thoughts, it begins to show on the face. And when that person has ugly thoughts every day, every week, every year, the face gets uglier and uglier until it gets so ugly you can hardly bear to look at it. <br><br>A person who has good thoughts cannot ever be ugly. You can have a wonky nose and a crooked mouth and a double chin and stick-out teeth, but if you have good thoughts they will shine out of your face like sunbeams and you will always look lovely."</i>
</blockquote>Now, where do I begin? Ah yes! Let's start with Mr. and Mrs. Twit. Well, I assure you, that both of them are a little bit, say, a few sandwiches short of a picnic or if you prefer something blunter, they're not one of the brightest bulbs on the Christmas tree. <br><br>Mr. Twit is a very bushy, nailbrushy-faced, grizzly old man who doesn't bother with his appearance.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542283702i/26601404.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I can't for the life of me understand why he'd rather bury himself in that grubby face of his. And please ladies and gentlemen, I implore you not to peer into that dreadful crevasse of moustachy bristles filled with mouldy and magotty morsels!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542283702i/26601405.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Mrs. Twit is just like Mr. Twit, but she's no better than him. She's as foul as his malodorous husband with a walking stick and a glass eye!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542283702i/26601406.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>They are one of the most hideous characters who'd exact revenge upon each other, given a chance.<blockquote>
  <i>"I'll swish you to a swazzle! I'll swash you to a swizzle! I'll gnash you to a gnozzle! I'll gnosh you to a gnazzle!"</i>
</blockquote>And if that wasn't enough for vengeance, there's this Giant Skillywiggler with teeth like screwdrivers, eat-me-up-while-its-hot Squiggly Spaghetti, the dreadful shrink, some Hugtight extraordinary glue for extra staying power — perfect for your Wednesday's Bird Pie supper! <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542283702i/26601407.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542283702i/26601408.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Or even Boy Pie supper for that matter, if you want to satiate your cannibalistic tendencies.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542283702i/26601409.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <i>"He's going to boil us!"<br>"He'll stew us alive!" <br>"He'll cook us with carrots!"</i>
</blockquote>Oh, what a fun way to bake some spoiled children! Errr... I beg your pardon, but that was my doppelgänger talking. I have to restrain him once more. <br><br>Now, on to the Twit's garden, we go!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542283702i/26601410.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>This two nasty couple keep Muggle-Wump and his family locked in a protective cage. This poor family are coerced to perform upside-down tricks for the Twit's amusement, including eating, dancing, playing, drinking, and all the jazz! What the Twits don't realize is that Muggle-Wump along with the Roly-Poly Bird is crafting a brilliant plan to get rid of them once and for all...<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/85916.The_Twits" title="The Twits by Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">The Twits</a> was truly an imaginative yet horrid tale filled with peculiar characters, unbridled wickedness, misanthropic undertones, playful wit, and clever word play — all done with cheeky humour! It seems that Dahl himself has a certain kind of aversion when it comes to unkempt appearance. Is Dahl implying that Mr. Twit needs some kind of manscaping or he isn't just fond of all that hairy mess? If you analyse further, he seems to be also discriminatory. Just look at Mrs. Twit's glass eye, which in reality you might call lazy eye or amblyopia. A case of lookism? The way he narrates this one too: <i>"But these were English birds and they couldn’t understand the weird African language the monkeys spoke."</i> A case of racism? As whimsical as this story might seem, there are bullying, toxic relationships, bias against idiots (thus the title), and revenge (is a dish best served cold). Well, that's only my hypotheses. Despite all that speculation, if you dig further and deeper, you'll find a hidden gem. And that is... the Golden Rule — a maxim we all know by heart and might be the heart of the story too! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10216085047512611152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12868045554291567494"><b>Unfortunately, I don't have any rose-tinted glasses for this one. </b><br/><br/>So, as an adult, all I could think of is, "<i>Dahl,</i> what were you <i>on</i>??"<blockquote>
  <i>Mr. Twit was a twit. He was born a twit. And, now at the age of sixty, he was a bigger twit than ever.</i>
</blockquote><b>The Twits are ugly people </b>- through and through. They think nothing of animal neglect or outright abuse. They are horrible to each other and everyone around them. <br/><br/>They own a troop of trained monkeys and take <b>particular delight</b> in forcing the poor animals into </span>
  <span id="freeText12868045554291567494" style="display:none"><b>Unfortunately, I don't have any rose-tinted glasses for this one. </b><br /><br />So, as an adult, all I could think of is, "<i>Dahl,</i> what were you <i>on</i>??"<blockquote>
  <i>Mr. Twit was a twit. He was born a twit. And, now at the age of sixty, he was a bigger twit than ever.</i>
</blockquote><b>The Twits are ugly people </b>- through and through. They think nothing of animal neglect or outright abuse. They are horrible to each other and everyone around them. <br /><br />They own a troop of trained monkeys and take <b>particular delight</b> in forcing the poor animals into doing <b>difficult (and painful) tricks. </b><br /><br />Well, the final straw landed on the camel's back (so to speak). The monkeys are fed up. They (along with a few friends) seek revenge through<b> creative and inventive methods.</b><br /><br />Much like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6670.The_Magic_Finger" title="The Magic Finger by Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic Finger</a>, the character's vengeance is swift, clever and almost disproportionately brutal. And while it was cute because the<b> animals were inventive</b> and the evil folks certainly got their comeuppance, it still had me raising my eyebrows.<br /><br /><b> Kids books were so not PG back in the day.</b><br /><br />I did, however, enjoy Dahl's level of pettiness. In real life, he hated beards. Thought them dirty and nasty. So, when he really wanted to convey just how disgusting the Twits were, he would throw in details like this:<blockquote>
  <i>By sticking out his tongue and curling it sideways to explore the hairy jungle around his mouth, he was always able to find a tasty morsel here and there to nibble on.</i>

<div id="review_209396181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/209396181" />
    <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence"><img alt="Mark Lawrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442536170p2/4508542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/209396181?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Lawrence" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence">Mark Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer209396181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16729745706002726852">I read a lot of Roald Dahl books as a child, and have read quite a few more to my own children, most recently to my disabled youngest daughter. The Twits was one of those.<br/><br/>The Twits, although it has its moments, is one of my least favourite Dahl books, perhaps <i>the</i> least favourite.<br/><br/>It's easy to be too po-faced about humour in children's books, and perhaps my reaction is coloured by the knowledge that Dahl was not a particularly pleasant man and had some rather nasty opinions ... but even so, my rea</span>
  <span id="freeText16729745706002726852" style="display:none">I read a lot of Roald Dahl books as a child, and have read quite a few more to my own children, most recently to my disabled youngest daughter. The Twits was one of those.<br /><br />The Twits, although it has its moments, is one of my least favourite Dahl books, perhaps <i>the</i> least favourite.<br /><br />It's easy to be too po-faced about humour in children's books, and perhaps my reaction is coloured by the knowledge that Dahl was not a particularly pleasant man and had some rather nasty opinions ... but even so, my reaction predates knowledge of his anti-Semitic views and other prejudices. And other of his books have not struck a sour chord with me in the same way.<br /><br />The book opens with a rather strange tirade against men with beards. But fair enough, it's just a fashion choice. What I found far less palatable as something being channeled into the heads of children was the assertion that ugly people are evil (have ugly thoughts). This is basically an extension of medieval thinking to the end that bad things happen to bad people and if misfortune befalls someone it's safe to assume that they had it coming.<br /><br />He says that if a person thinks good thoughts it will "shine through" and even if they have features that are technically ugly we will see just by looking that they are a nice person. This is of course bollocks, and not just that, it's dangerous bollocks, and should not be told to children. <br /><br />The idea that someone who looks ugly to us is ugly inside too is sufficient reason on its own to cast this book aside.<br /><br />A fuller discussion can be found here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://mark---lawrence.blogspot.com/2018/02/lets-not-be-twits.html">http://mark---lawrence.blogspot.com/2...</a><br /><br />Moving on.<br /><br />The rest of the book comprises two unpleasant people being unpleasant to each other in not particularly humorous ways, followed by the addition of monkeys and a magical bird who then outwit them in a rather unconvincing manner.<br /><br />I really was not taken with the story, but it wasn't terrible. Give me James and the Giant Peach, Charlie and the Chocolate Factory, or The Fantastic Mr Fox any day. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br /><br /><br />....</span>
  <a data-text-id="16729745706002726852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9588161140992274514">ENGLISH (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31456.The_Twits' title='The Twits by Roald Dahl' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Twits</a>)/ ITALIANO<br/><br/><blockquote>«What a lot of hairy-faced men there are around nowadays»</blockquote>Ugly, dirty and bad. We are talking, instead, about the Twits, Mr and Mrs Twits, spending their days tremendously pranking each other with jokes of unnecessary cruelty. Mr Twits, moreover, has his own dreams: training monkeys to carry out acts upside down. In short, the Twits are evil.<p>But revenge comes as a ju</p></span>
  <span id="freeText9588161140992274514" style="display:none">ENGLISH (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31456.The_Twits" title="The Twits by Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">The Twits</a>)/ ITALIANO<br><br><blockquote>«What a lot of hairy-faced men there are around nowadays»</blockquote>Ugly, dirty and bad. It's not about the movie of Ettore Scola about the slums, with Nino Manfredi as memorable protagonist. We are talking, instead, about the Twits, Mr and Mrs Twits, spending their days tremendously pranking each other with jokes of unnecessary cruelty. Mr Twits, moreover, has his own dreams: training monkeys to carry out acts upside down. In short, the Twits are evil.<p>But revenge comes as a judgment.</p><p>Vote: 7.5</p><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1540235067i/26484749._SX540_.jpg" width="420" height="315" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>«Quanti uomini con la faccia pelosa ci sono in giro al giorno d'oggi»</blockquote>Brutti, sporchi e cattivi. Insomma, perfidie su perfidie.<p>Ma la vendetta arriva lapidaria.</p><p>Voto: 7,5</p></span>

<div id="review_2444416359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2444416359" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2444416359?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142410394" href="/book/show/85916.The_Twits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=children-of-all-ages">children-of-all-ages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=3-star-reads">3-star-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2444416359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15437723926689763910"><i>“If a person has ugly thoughts, it begins to show on the face. And when that person has ugly thoughts every day, every week, every year, the face gets uglier and uglier until you can hardly bear to look at it.<br/><br/>A person who has good thoughts cannot ever be ugly. You can have a wonky nose and a crooked mouth and a double chin and stick-out teeth, but if you have good thoughts it will shine out of your face like sunbeams and you will always look lovely.” </i><br/><br/>I do love this quote. <i>The Twits</i> are the epito</span>
  <span id="freeText15437723926689763910" style="display:none"><i>“If a person has ugly thoughts, it begins to show on the face. And when that person has ugly thoughts every day, every week, every year, the face gets uglier and uglier until you can hardly bear to look at it.<br /><br />A person who has good thoughts cannot ever be ugly. You can have a wonky nose and a crooked mouth and a double chin and stick-out teeth, but if you have good thoughts it will shine out of your face like sunbeams and you will always look lovely.” </i><br /><br />I do love this quote. <i>The Twits</i> are the epitome of nastiness and everything a person shouldn’t be. They are vile and small, silly little people that enjoy inflicting pain on others for no reason other than their own amusement.<br /><br />So in typical Roald Dahl fashion they get exactly what is coming to them. They may be caricatures, though they are a very good example to children about why we should never hate. Even though they are horrible, hating them is the wrong thing to do because we are just as bad as them. Toxic people should be removed from our lives. There’s no point hating them, just walk away from them like the animals attempt to do here.<br /><br />That being said, why does Roald Dahl hate beards so much? You'd think he'd heed his own words.</span>

<div id="review_194855972" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194855972" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194855972?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Matt by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/22371819-mariah-roze">Mariah Roze</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194855972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1611561292044956244">Another re-read for the fun of it!<br/><br/>This story pulls the reader to the edge, injecting silliness, fear, and all-around revenge into a larger plot that will have children giggling and washing their faces in short order. What is a twit? Not so easy to explain, is it? Well, Dahl seeks to provide the reader with a slight understanding by offering up some of their hygienic deficiencies (especially among the men whose hairy faces are receptacles for anything that could land therein), persistent ugliness</span>
  <span id="freeText1611561292044956244" style="display:none">Another re-read for the fun of it!<br /><br />This story pulls the reader to the edge, injecting silliness, fear, and all-around revenge into a larger plot that will have children giggling and washing their faces in short order. What is a twit? Not so easy to explain, is it? Well, Dahl seeks to provide the reader with a slight understanding by offering up some of their hygienic deficiencies (especially among the men whose hairy faces are receptacles for anything that could land therein), persistent ugliness (which stems from thoughts of that nature), and utter disregard for anyone else. However, the greatest (worst?) trait of a twit would be their incessant need to seek revenge. Mr. and Mrs. Twit find themselves always trying to out-revenge one another, their hatred surely having been cemented into their wedding vows. One thing about which they agree wholeheartedly, though, is a love of Wednesday bird pies, and Mr. Twit has concocted a way to ensure his crust is always full of a variety of birds. Painting a super-sticky glue to the branches of his dead tree, Mr. Twit is able to trap many flying friends and eventually stuffs them into his rotting gullet. One day the Twits head out to handle an errand, at which time the local avian community teams up with some of the pet monkeys belonging to the Twits and the end result is the ultimate revenge. However, to outwit a Twit takes more than simple cunning, as the reader will soon learn. Perhaps of the great shorter stories of Dahl's that I have read since returning to him so many years later. Well crafted with all of the traditional Dahl wit and attempts at child-based humour. Worth a read, but perhaps not too late into the evening for the younger ones.<br /><br />Dahl reminds me (loosely) of a children's Stephen King, in that he is so full of ideas that are seemingly independent of one another, yet have loose threads that connect, at least for the attentive reader. Dahl is able to dazzle the reader with his array of spooky adult characters (another usual trait for Dahl books in that adults are most often evil or oppressive to the child in the story) and their antics to bestow revenge or pain on others. Dahl weaves the story from the early exploration of the Twits to the ultimate battle between good and evil (in this case fauna versus Twit) and there is little hope that it will end peacefully. Children can attach themselves to the ever-evolving narrative and laugh at key moments throughout. A wordsmith and gifted storyteller for sure, Dahl is in a class all his own.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Dahl for scaring us silly at times and making us laugh three pages later. I am sure Neo will love these books when he is a little older. If not, I will enjoy them for him!<br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1611561292044956244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12698910602724960221">Twits are ugly people who do horrible things to each other and others. They are not nice, and they are negative people who have been negative so long that the negativity has made them ugly. <br/><br/>On Monday I was going to write a review that just said that I'm a twit. Which isn't really true, I'm generally a only a slightly negative person, bordering on neutral and I don't do things intentionally to try to cause other people harm. Sometimes I do turn incredibly negative though and then I come out swing</span>
  <span id="freeText12698910602724960221" style="display:none">Twits are ugly people who do horrible things to each other and others. They are not nice, and they are negative people who have been negative so long that the negativity has made them ugly. <br /><br />On Monday I was going to write a review that just said that I'm a twit. Which isn't really true, I'm generally a only a slightly negative person, bordering on neutral and I don't do things intentionally to try to cause other people harm. Sometimes I do turn incredibly negative though and then I come out swinging at anyone close to me. I get angry, feel incredibly destructive, make life hell for anyone nearby and then it passes and I just get really depressed for awhile. I hope, even when I'm in my shit mood, that I don't do anything to hurt anyone else in anyway, so I guess I'm not quite a Twit.<br /><br />Instead, I guess I unintentionally wait to wade through the bullshit of my depression, and do something then to fuck everything up, or at least start a chain reaction. Yay me, huh? <br /><br /><s>Don't vote for this</s>. I meant to say, <b>Vote for This</b>. Who cares if it's not a review. I generally don't write reviews, I write opinion pieces and rants peppered with confessionals from my life. Sometimes I write very critical things, and I guess they might be considered a review, but really they are just throwing venom and spite at a target that won't swing back. Very few of the many words I've used on this site are anything that would really give someone a sense if they want to read a book or not. <br /><br />That said, the book is amusing. You might like it. </span>

<div id="review_242997496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242997496" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242997496?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/8882025-the-twits">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242997496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7355336965201849292">Who doesn’t love a good villain? And Mr and Mrs Twit are a delightfully nasty pair! When they’re not having a go at one another - she mixing in live worms into his spaghetti, he trying to send her off into space with balloons - they’re trying to eat children, actually eating the local bird populace and torturing a family of monkeys. Then one day the monkeys decide to push back… <br/><br/>The Twits still holds up as one of my favourite Roald Dahl books. Dahl’s speciality is over-the-top baddies and he deli</span>
  <span id="freeText7355336965201849292" style="display:none">Who doesn’t love a good villain? And Mr and Mrs Twit are a delightfully nasty pair! When they’re not having a go at one another - she mixing in live worms into his spaghetti, he trying to send her off into space with balloons - they’re trying to eat children, actually eating the local bird populace and torturing a family of monkeys. Then one day the monkeys decide to push back… <br /><br />The Twits still holds up as one of my favourite Roald Dahl books. Dahl’s speciality is over-the-top baddies and he delivers with Mr and Mrs Twit who’re as grotesque as can be. Quentin Blake’s illustrations are perfect as always - his art is as inseparable from Dahl’s prose as John Tenniel’s is from Lewis Carroll’s. <br /><br />A few key plot points are perhaps a bit too easily glossed over, perhaps because Dahl is writing for a younger audience than his longer books like Matilda and The Witches - it is a much shorter book than either and feels a bit rushed towards the end. <br /><br />And the monkeys are a bit underwritten compared to the title characters. It’s a similar setup to Fantastic Mr Fox except, whereas Boggis, Bunce and Bean are as wonderfully vicious as Mr and Mrs Twit, the monkeys and the Roly-Poly Bird are nowhere near as fully realised as Mr Fox, his family and friends. <br /><br />Still, the story remains ingenious fun even some 25+ years since I last read this as a kid. And I also think there’s some truth in thinking cruel and wicked thoughts warping your outward appearance over time. Be good, everyone, inside and out! The Twits: a brilliant book about a couple of eminently hateable scumbags! </span>
  <a data-text-id="7355336965201849292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1032757650" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1032757650" />
    <a title="Anthony Vacca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27183668-anthony-vacca"><img alt="Anthony Vacca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604067844p2/27183668.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1032757650?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Vacca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Vacca" href="/user/show/27183668-anthony-vacca">Anthony Vacca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032757650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13138099893941415345">Dahl's <i>The Twits</i> is at its finest during the first half of the book which relates various highlights in the comedy of cruelty that is the marriage between the two eponymous grotesques, Mr and Mrs Twit. When Mrs Twit isn't serving Mr Twit a bowl of worms or hiding her glass eye in his after-supper beer, and when Mr Twit isn't playing a fucked-up mind game on Mrs Twit - such as carving away an inch of his wife's cane, day by day, so that he can trick her into thinking she is slowly but surely shri</span>
  <span id="freeText13138099893941415345" style="display:none">Dahl's <i>The Twits</i> is at its finest during the first half of the book which relates various highlights in the comedy of cruelty that is the marriage between the two eponymous grotesques, Mr and Mrs Twit. When Mrs Twit isn't serving Mr Twit a bowl of worms or hiding her glass eye in his after-supper beer, and when Mr Twit isn't playing a fucked-up mind game on Mrs Twit - such as carving away an inch of his wife's cane, day by day, so that he can trick her into thinking she is slowly but surely shrinking - the two put their loathsome heads together to terrorize monkeys, butcher birds, and even try their hand at eating little boys. The second half of the book is gentler and more playful with its many exotic animals banding together to make sure that the Twits get the their topsy-turvy just desserts. I for one would have loved for hundreds of more pages of Panurgian acts of vengeance between the two utterly reprehensible and revolting Twits, but we must remember the kids, of course.<br /><br />Dahl once again serves up another irreverently funny story for the more astute and world-weary young readers of the world. <i>The Twits</i> is a sound reminder that the world is full of mostly awful people who will do mostly awful things to other people, like you for instance little boy and/or girl. <br /><br />The voluble, pitch-black satirist Will Self recommended this wonderful audio recording of the book which features actor Simon Callow giving absolutely disgusting and brilliant voices to the titular twits (the only downside is that you lose out on Quentin Blake's idiosyncratically iconic illustrations): <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fJzlPT_-Vwc">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fJzlP...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13138099893941415345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111745799-edgarr-alien-pooh?shelf=kids">kids</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3385772602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6626911217371206078">The Twits by Roald Dahl is the usual funny and clever fare that we get from this much-celebrated author. A short read it is about a married couple, The Twits, who rarely see eye to eye, plainly don't get along and lead sad, miserable lives which they feel the need to take out on the rest of the world.<br/><br/>To show the brilliance of Dahl as an author is easy. The Twits, as a couple, are offensive, unkind and plain rude yet the read is fun and enjoyable. Some of the content nobody else could get away wi</span>
  <span id="freeText6626911217371206078" style="display:none">The Twits by Roald Dahl is the usual funny and clever fare that we get from this much-celebrated author. A short read it is about a married couple, The Twits, who rarely see eye to eye, plainly don't get along and lead sad, miserable lives which they feel the need to take out on the rest of the world.<br /><br />To show the brilliance of Dahl as an author is easy. The Twits, as a couple, are offensive, unkind and plain rude yet the read is fun and enjoyable. Some of the content nobody else could get away with because it borders on abusive yet there is no malice in the writing at all. This is a couple that you would neither want to be nor live close to yet from a distance they are a great laugh. Perhaps the greatest part of the story is the triumph of the animals over The Twits, not a spoiler as you know it is headed there from the start, but only Dahl can write such a special demise - think of the children who don't make it to the end of Charlie and the Chocolate Factory.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6626911217371206078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1117616868427207372">One of my favourite books.<br/>A lil gruesome but so funny. A sheer delight to read.<br/>Such a memorable book. I will treasure.</span>

  <span id="freeText16812377652719655468" style="display:none">Funny childish story of a couple who do nasty things to each other and the birds and the monkeys.   <span id="freeText14969025861407860107" style="display:none"><b>A simply dreadful story about Mr and Mrs Twit.</b><br /> <br />They play pranks on each other; such as worms in food, frogs in beds, psychological torture, and air space incursions.<br />They catch and cook all types of British birds without checking to see if any are nearly extinct.<br />They try to catch, cook and eat young boys.<br />They force a family of monkeys to perform horrible tricks that endanger the monkeys' health.<br />They buy shotguns without a license, and intend to shoot inside a suburb.<br /><br />That is what a politically correct reviewer from the nanny state would say before banning the book. But not children!<br /><br />I have read this story to many of my junior classes, who simply adored the antics of the Twits and the monkeys' revenge.<br /><br /><i>Don't tell the nanny state inspectors, but this story is Horribly Funny.</i><br /><br />Enjoy!</span>

  <span id="freeText12429836224236465030" style="display:none">It’s always refreshing to read a Dahl book, he’s definitely one of My favorite authors. It’s just nice to be able to sit back and laugh and read a solid book that doesn’t pander or worry about nothing, he always hits the sweet spot. Dahl rules &amp; the twits is a great read and funny too!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1655990058" />
    <a title="Shaina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49002481-shaina"><img alt="Shaina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596530962p2/49002481.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655990058?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140346404" href="/book/show/980151.The_Twits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49002481-shaina?shelf=bargains-lib-daily-deals-onsale">bargains-lib-daily-deals-onsale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49002481-shaina?shelf=children-s-nostalgia">children-s-nostalgia</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49002481-shaina?shelf=used">used</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1655990058&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655990058" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10370152210406572768">Loved it! Humorous, doesn’t tip toe around and is full on Roald Dahl! <br/><br/>I love the illustrations a lot, but don’t look for pretty! Look for exactly what the story is talking about. It can be kinda gross, but interesting and really challenges illustration. They are for more than just the “pretty”. <br/> <br/>My favorite moral, besides help one another? <br/><br/>If you act ugly and behave ugly, it makes you ugly and that is all! Otherwise you are fine and I love that !!! <br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1599109969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1599109969" />
    <a title="Joey Woolfardis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4639825-joey-woolfardis"><img alt="Joey Woolfardis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490696206p2/4639825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1599109969?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joey Woolfardis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joey Woolfardis" href="/user/show/4639825-joey-woolfardis">Joey Woolfardis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142410394" href="/book/show/85916.The_Twits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=ce20">ce20</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=bookshelf">bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=masculine">masculine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=bairns">bairns</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=intriguing-but-ultimately-naff">intriguing-but-ultimately-naff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1599109969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7979322853763455530">Read as part of <a href='https://infiniteanddarling.co.uk/blogs/infinite-variety-books/the-infinite-variety-reading-challenge-part-one' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Infinite Variety Reading Challenge</a>, based on the BBC's Big Read Poll of 2003.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>"A person who has good thoughts cannot ever be ugly. You can have a wonky nose and a crooked mouth and a double chin and stick-out teeth, but if you have good thoughts they will shine out of your face like sunbeams and you will always look lovely."</b>
</i><br/><br/><i>The Twits</i> is one of the more well-known Roald Dahl books that I didn't know anything about and I can't say that's a bad thing. It's a fairly decent yar</span>
  <span id="freeText7979322853763455530" style="display:none">Read as part of <a href="https://infiniteanddarling.co.uk/blogs/infinite-variety-books/the-infinite-variety-reading-challenge-part-one" rel="nofollow noopener">The Infinite Variety Reading Challenge</a>, based on the BBC's Big Read Poll of 2003.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"A person who has good thoughts cannot ever be ugly. You can have a wonky nose and a crooked mouth and a double chin and stick-out teeth, but if you have good thoughts they will shine out of your face like sunbeams and you will always look lovely."</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>The Twits</i> is one of the more well-known Roald Dahl books that I didn't know anything about and I can't say that's a bad thing. It's a fairly decent yarn about some horrible couple who are horrible to themselves, each other and anything within a five-thousand-mile-radius but it completely lacks a solid plot and the adventurous whimsy of his other works.<br /><br />Dahl didn't like beards at all, which I think tells you everything you need to know.<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.infiniteanddarling.co.uk/blogs/infinite-variety-books" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/infiniteANDdarling/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/infinitedarlin" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://uk.pinterest.com/infinitedarling/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> | <a href="https://www.infiniteanddarling.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Shop</a> | <a href="https://www.etsy.com/uk/shop/infiniteANDdarling" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7979322853763455530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=children-s-book">children-s-book</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=illustrations">illustrations</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212235710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1456016743666371487">Quite funny and entertaining, not as good as <i>The BFG</i> or <i>Matilda</i> though.<br/><br/>I kind of loved Mr and Mrs Twit, despite them being horrible to everyone. I thought the nasty tricks they played on each other and names they called each other were actually kind of cute, they both were just so well suited each other (unlike most fictional couples). They might just be my OTP.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8w358KZjlocbTdnwLO/d+9UOX+7dP1uhpuSme9Cvm67JK5AiHT1f77xmbZHbGtckA1G4JhOy1cb9muDKHexpNA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('v6VkAtjoJ3uvoaYV6QSvDFsOgOuFK5aC8ibNDEqMwwSFgw3QY7buEwiKEnQe8aXTjVFnI0umGOWpWIu9h88xng==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl">About Roald Dahl</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9374327872364844037">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br/><br/>Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was <i>Shot Down Over Libya</i>. Today the story is published as <i>A Piece of Cake</i>. The story, about his wartime adv</span>
  <span id="freeText9374327872364844037" style="display:none">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br /><br />Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was <i>Shot Down Over Libya</i>. Today the story is published as <i>A Piece of Cake</i>. The story, about his wartime adventures, was bought by the Saturday Evening Post for $900, and propelled him into a career as a writer. Its title was inspired by a highly inaccurate and sensationalized article about the crash that blinded him, which claimed he had been shot down instead of simply having to land because of low fuel.<br /><br />His first children's book was <i>The Gremlins</i>, about mischievous little creatures that were part of RAF folklore. The book was commissioned by Walt Disney for a film that was never made, and published in 1943. Dahl went on to create some of the best-loved children's stories of the 20th century, such as <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, <i>Matilda</i> and <i>James and the Giant Peach</i>.<br /><br />He also had a successful parallel career as the writer of macabre adult short stories, usually with a dark sense of humour and a surprise ending. Many were originally written for American magazines such as <i>Ladies Home Journal</i>, <i>Harper's</i>, <i>Playboy</i> and <i>The New Yorker</i>, then subsequently collected by Dahl into anthologies, gaining world-wide acclaim. Dahl wrote more than 60 short stories and they have appeared in numerous collections, some only being published in book form after his death. His stories also brought him three Edgar Awards: in 1954, for the collection <i>Someone Like You</i>; in 1959, for the story "The Landlady"; and in 1980, for the episode of <i>Tales of the Unexpected</i> based on "Skin".</span>
  <a data-text-id="9374327872364844037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
